<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Short-life_engine" title="Short-life engine">Short-life engine</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Students_from_Kashan_on_Rahian-e-Pishraft_Tour_(11).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Students_from_Kashan_on_Rahian-e-Pishraft_Tour_%2811%29.jpg/250px-Students_from_Kashan_on_Rahian-e-Pishraft_Tour_%2811%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Students_from_Kashan_on_Rahian-e-Pishraft_Tour_%2811%29.jpg/500px-Students_from_Kashan_on_Rahian-e-Pishraft_Tour_%2811%29.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="1300" data-file-height="867" /></a><figcaption>Rear view of the Iranian <a href="/wiki/Shahed_149_Gaza" title="Shahed 149 Gaza">Shahed 149 Gaza</a> UCAV</figcaption></figure>
<p>Traditional <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion" class="mw-redirect" title="Internal combustion">internal combustion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jet_engine" title="Jet engine">jet engines</a> remain in use for drones requiring long range. However, for shorter-range missions electric power has almost entirely taken over. The distance record for a UAV (built from balsa wood and mylar skin) across the North Atlantic Ocean is held by a gasoline model airplane or UAV. Manard Hill "in 2003 when one of his creations flew 1,882 miles across the Atlantic Ocean on less than a gallon of fuel" holds this record.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Besides the traditional piston engine, the <a href="/wiki/Wankel_rotary_engine" class="mw-redirect" title="Wankel rotary engine">Wankel rotary engine</a> is used by some drones. This type offers high power output for lower weight, with quieter and more vibration-free running. Claims have also been made for improved reliability and greater range.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="not cited elsewhere (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Small drones mostly use <a href="/wiki/Lithium_polymer_battery" title="Lithium polymer battery">lithium-polymer batteries</a> (Li-Po)<sup id="cite&#95;ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>, while some larger vehicles have adopted the <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_fuel_cell" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydrogen fuel cell">hydrogen fuel cell</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-auto&#95;116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">Hydrogen</a>-fueled <a href="/wiki/Proton-exchange_membrane_fuel_cell" title="Proton-exchange membrane fuel cell">proton-exchange membrane fuel cells</a> for UAVs have the advantages of longer flight duration than rechargeable <a href="/wiki/Lithium-ion_batteries" class="mw-redirect" title="Lithium-ion batteries">lithium-ion batteries</a>, of lower <a href="/wiki/Total_cost_of_ownership" title="Total cost of ownership">total cost of ownership</a> than primary <a href="/wiki/Lithium_metal_batteries" class="mw-redirect" title="Lithium metal batteries">lithium metal batteries</a> and of better stealth than <a href="/wiki/Heat_engines" class="mw-redirect" title="Heat engines">heat engines</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-auto3&#95;36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto3-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The energy density of modern Li-Po batteries is far less than gasoline or hydrogen. However, electric motors are cheaper, lighter and quieter. Complex multi-engine, multi-propeller installations are under development with the goal of improving aerodynamic and propulsive efficiency. For such complex power installations, <a href="/wiki/Battery_eliminator_circuit" title="Battery eliminator circuit">battery elimination circuitry</a> (BEC) may be used to centralize power distribution and minimize heating, under the control of a <a href="/wiki/Microcontroller" title="Microcontroller">microcontroller unit</a> (MCU).
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Ornithopters_–_wing_propulsion"><span id="Ornithopters_.E2.80.93_wing_propulsion"></span>Ornithopters – wing propulsion</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Ornithopters – wing propulsion"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Flapping-wing <a href="/wiki/Ornithopter" title="Ornithopter">ornithopters</a>, imitating birds or insects, have been flown as <a href="/wiki/Micro_air_vehicle" title="Micro air vehicle">microUAVs</a>. Their inherent stealth recommends them for spy missions.
</p><p>Sub-1g microUAVs inspired by flies, albeit using a power tether, have been able to "land" on vertical surfaces.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Other projects mimic the flight of beetles and other insects.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Computer_control_systems">Computer control systems</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Computer control systems"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:AbuseMark_AfroFlight_Naze_32_Flight_Controller_rev5_white.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/AbuseMark_AfroFlight_Naze_32_Flight_Controller_rev5_white.jpg/500px-AbuseMark_AfroFlight_Naze_32_Flight_Controller_rev5_white.jpg" decoding="async" width="340" height="173" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/AbuseMark_AfroFlight_Naze_32_Flight_Controller_rev5_white.jpg/960px-AbuseMark_AfroFlight_Naze_32_Flight_Controller_rev5_white.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="6300" data-file-height="3200" /></a><figcaption>A flight controller run on either CleanFlight or BaseFlight firmware for <a href="/wiki/Multirotor" title="Multirotor">multirotor</a> UAVs</figcaption></figure>
<p>UAV computing capability followed the advances of computing technology, beginning with analog controls and evolving into microcontrollers, then <a href="/wiki/System_on_a_chip" title="System on a chip">system-on-a-chip</a> (SOC) and <a href="/wiki/Single-board_computer" title="Single-board computer">single-board computers</a> (SBC).
</p><p>Modern system hardware for UAV control is often called the flight controller (FC), flight controller board (FCB) or autopilot. Common UAV-systems control hardware typically incorporate a primary microprocessor, a secondary or failsafe processor, and sensors such as accelerometers, gyroscopes, magnetometers, and barometers into a single module.
</p><p>In 2024 EASA agreed on the first certification basis for a UAV flight controller in compliance with the ETSO-C198 for Embention's autopilot. The certification of the UAV flight control systems aims to facilitate the integration of UAVs within the airspace and the operation of drones in critical areas.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Architecture">Architecture</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Architecture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Sensors">Sensors</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Sensors"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Position and movement sensors give information about the aircraft state. Exteroceptive sensors deal with external information like distance measurements, while exproprioceptive ones correlate internal and external states.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Nature&#95;-&#95;Future&#95;of&#95;sUAVs&#95;120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nature_-_Future_of_sUAVs-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Non-cooperative sensors are able to detect targets autonomously so they are used for separation assurance and collision avoidance.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Degrees of freedom (DOF) refers to both the amount and quality of onboard sensors: 6 DOF implies 3-axis gyroscopes and accelerometers (a typical <a href="/wiki/Inertial_measurement_unit" title="Inertial measurement unit">inertial measurement unit</a>&#160;&#8211;&#32; IMU), 9 DOF refers to an IMU plus a compass, 10 DOF adds a barometer and 11 DOF usually adds a GPS receiver.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In addition to the navigation sensors, the UAV (or UAS) can be also equipped with monitoring devices such as: <a href="/wiki/RGB_color_model" title="RGB color model">RGB</a>, <a href="/wiki/Multispectral_imaging" title="Multispectral imaging">multispectral</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyperspectral_imaging" title="Hyperspectral imaging">hyper-spectral</a> cameras or <a href="/wiki/Lidar" title="Lidar">LiDAR</a>, which may allow providing specific measurements or observations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Actuators">Actuators</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Actuators"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>UAV <a href="/wiki/Actuator" title="Actuator">actuators</a> include <a href="/wiki/Electronic_speed_control" title="Electronic speed control">digital electronic speed controllers</a> (which control the <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_per_minute" title="Revolutions per minute">RPM</a> of the motors) linked to motors/<a href="/wiki/Engine" title="Engine">engines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Propeller" title="Propeller">propellers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Servomotor" title="Servomotor">servomotors</a> (for planes and helicopters mostly), weapons, payload actuators, LEDs and speakers.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2025)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Software">Software</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Software"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Modern UAVs run a software stack that ranges from low-level firmware that directly controls actuators, to high level flight planning. At the lowest level, firmware directly controls reading from sensors such as an <a href="/wiki/Inertial_measurement_unit" title="Inertial measurement unit">IMU</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and commanding actuators such as motors. Control software (often referred to as an autopilot) is responsible for computing actuator speeds given desired vehicle velocity. Due to its direct interaction with hardware, this software is time-critical and may run on <a href="/wiki/Microcontroller" title="Microcontroller">microcontrollers</a>. This software may also handle radio communications, in the case of UAVs that are not autonomous. One popular example is the PX4 autopilot.
</p><p>At the next level, autonomy algorithms compute the desired velocity given higher level goals. For example, <a href="/wiki/Trajectory_optimization" title="Trajectory optimization">trajectory optimization</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> may be used to calculate a flight trajectory given a desired goal location. This software is not necessarily time-critical, and can often run on a single board computer running an operating system such as <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a> with relaxed time constraints.
</p><p>Deep reinforcement learning has also been investigated for UAV flight control, particularly for navigating continuous three-dimensional environments and improving autonomous decision-making.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Similarly, AI-driven automation is increasingly being applied to counter-UAS (C-UAS) systems to reduce operator cognitive load by automatically linking electronic drone detection data with physical tracking cameras for "hands-free" target tracking.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-auto2&#95;127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-127"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Loop_principles">Loop principles</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Loop principles"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:UAV_Flight_control.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/UAV_Flight_control.jpg/250px-UAV_Flight_control.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="213" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/UAV_Flight_control.jpg/500px-UAV_Flight_control.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="623" data-file-height="531" /></a><figcaption>Typical flight-control loops for a multirotor</figcaption></figure>
<p>UAVs employ open-loop, closed-loop or hybrid control architectures.
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Open-loop_controller" title="Open-loop controller">Open loop</a>&#160;&#8211;&#32; This type provides a positive control signal (faster, slower, left, right, up, down) without incorporating feedback from sensor data.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Closed-loop_transfer_function" title="Closed-loop transfer function">Closed loop</a>&#160;&#8211;&#32; This type incorporates sensor feedback to adjust behavior (reduce speed to reflect tailwind, move to altitude 300 feet). The <a href="/wiki/PID_controller" class="mw-redirect" title="PID controller">PID controller</a> is common. Sometimes, <a href="/wiki/Feed_forward_(control)" title="Feed forward (control)">feedforward</a> is employed, transferring the need to close the loop further.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Communications">Communications</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Communications"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>UAVs use a <a href="/wiki/Radio" title="Radio">radio</a> for control and <a href="/wiki/Data_link" title="Data link">exchange of video and other data</a>. Early UAVs had only <a href="/wiki/Narrowband" title="Narrowband">narrowband</a> uplink. Downlinks came later. These bi-directional narrowband radio links carried command and control (C&amp;C) and <a href="/wiki/Telemetry" title="Telemetry">telemetry</a> data about the status of aircraft systems to the remote operator.
</p><p>In most modern UAV applications, video transmission is required. So instead of having separate links for C&amp;C, telemetry and video traffic, a <a href="/wiki/Broadband" title="Broadband">broadband</a> link is used to carry all types of data. These broadband links can leverage <a href="/wiki/Quality_of_service" title="Quality of service">quality of service</a> techniques and carry <a href="/wiki/TCP/IP" class="mw-redirect" title="TCP/IP">TCP/IP</a> traffic that can be routed over the internet.
</p><p>The radio signal from the operator side can be issued from either:
</p>
<ul><li>Ground control – a human operating a <a href="/wiki/Transmitter" title="Transmitter">radio transmitter</a>/receiver, a smartphone, a tablet, a computer, or the original meaning of a <a href="/wiki/UAV_ground_control_station" title="UAV ground control station">military ground control station (GCS)</a>.</li>
<li>Remote network system, such as satellite duplex data links for some <a href="/wiki/Armed_forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Armed forces">military powers</a>. Downstream digital video over mobile networks has also entered consumer markets, while direct UAV control uplink over the cellular mesh and LTE have been demonstrated and are in trials.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>129<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Another aircraft, serving as a relay or mobile control station&#160;&#8211;&#32; military manned-unmanned teaming (MUM-T).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>130<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Modern networking standards have explicitly considered drones and therefore include optimizations. The 5G standard has mandated reduced user plane latency to 1ms while using ultra-reliable and low-latency communications.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>131<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>UAV-to-UAV coordination supported by <a href="/wiki/Remote_ID" title="Remote ID">Remote ID</a> communication technology. Remote ID messages (containing the UAV coordinates) are broadcast and can be used for collision-free navigation.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Autonomy">Autonomy</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Autonomy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_aircraft" title="Autonomous aircraft">Autonomous aircraft</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Degrees_of_autonomy.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Degrees_of_autonomy.jpg/250px-Degrees_of_autonomy.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="183" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Degrees_of_autonomy.jpg/500px-Degrees_of_autonomy.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="563" /></a><figcaption>UAV's degrees of autonomy</figcaption></figure>
<p>The level of autonomy in UAVs varies widely. UAV manufacturers often build in specific autonomous operations, such as:<sup id="cite&#95;ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>133<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Self-level: attitude stabilization on the pitch and roll axes.</li>
<li>Altitude hold: The aircraft maintains its altitude using barometric pressure and/or GPS data.</li>
<li>Hover/position hold: Keep level pitch and roll, stable yaw heading and altitude while maintaining position using <a href="/wiki/GNSS" class="mw-redirect" title="GNSS">GNSS</a> or inertial sensors.</li>
<li>Headless mode: Pitch control relative to the position of the pilot rather than relative to the vehicle's axes.</li>
<li>Care-free: automatic roll and yaw control while moving horizontally</li>
<li>Takeoff and landing (using a variety of aircraft or ground-based sensors and systems; see also "<a href="/wiki/Autoland" title="Autoland">autoland</a>")</li>
<li>Failsafe: automatic landing or return-to-home upon loss of control signal</li>
<li>Return-to-home: Fly back to the point of takeoff (often gaining altitude first to avoid possible intervening obstructions such as trees or buildings).</li>
<li>Follow-me: Maintain relative position to a moving pilot or other object using GNSS, <a href="/wiki/Image_recognition" class="mw-redirect" title="Image recognition">image recognition</a> or homing beacon.</li>
<li>GPS waypoint navigation: Using GNSS to navigate to an intermediate location on a travel path.</li>
<li>Orbit around an object: Similar to Follow-me but continuously circle a target.</li>
<li>Pre-programmed <a href="/wiki/Aerobatics" title="Aerobatics">aerobatics</a> (such as rolls and loops)</li>
<li>Pre-programmed delivery (delivery drones)</li></ul>
<p>One approach to quantifying autonomous capabilities is based on <a href="/wiki/OODA_loop" title="OODA loop">OODA</a> terminology, as suggested by a 2002 US <a href="/wiki/Air_Force_Research_Laboratory" title="Air Force Research Laboratory">Air Force Research Laboratory</a> report, and used in the table on the right.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>134<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:X-47B_receives_fuel_from_an_Omega_K-707_tanker_while_operating_in_the_Atlantic_Test_Ranges.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/X-47B_receives_fuel_from_an_Omega_K-707_tanker_while_operating_in_the_Atlantic_Test_Ranges.jpg/250px-X-47B_receives_fuel_from_an_Omega_K-707_tanker_while_operating_in_the_Atlantic_Test_Ranges.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/X-47B_receives_fuel_from_an_Omega_K-707_tanker_while_operating_in_the_Atlantic_Test_Ranges.jpg/500px-X-47B_receives_fuel_from_an_Omega_K-707_tanker_while_operating_in_the_Atlantic_Test_Ranges.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="4240" data-file-height="2830" /></a><figcaption>A <a href="/wiki/Northrop_Grumman_X-47B" title="Northrop Grumman X-47B">Northrop Grumman X-47B</a> unmanned combat aircraft demonstrator of the US Navy refuels in flight from a tanker aircraft.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Full autonomy is available for specific tasks, such as <a href="/wiki/Airborne_refueling" class="mw-redirect" title="Airborne refueling">airborne refueling</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>135<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> or ground-based battery switching.
</p><p>Other functions available or under development include; collective flight, real-time <a href="/wiki/Collision_avoidance_system" title="Collision avoidance system">collision avoidance</a>, wall following, corridor centring, simultaneous localization and mapping and <a href="/wiki/Swarm_robotics" title="Swarm robotics">swarming</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>136<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_radio" title="Cognitive radio">cognitive radio</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Machine_learning" title="Machine learning">machine learning</a>. In this context, <a href="/wiki/Computer_vision" title="Computer vision">computer vision</a> can play an important role for automatically ensuring flight safety.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Performance_considerations">Performance considerations</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Performance considerations"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Flight_envelope">Flight envelope</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Flight envelope"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>UAVs can be programmed to perform aggressive maneuvers or landing/perching on inclined surfaces,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>137<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and then to climb toward better communication spots.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>138<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Some UAVs can control flight with varying flight modelisation,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>139<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> such as VTOL designs.
</p><p>UAVs can also implement perching on a flat vertical surface.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>141<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Endurance">Endurance</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Endurance"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:UAV-741-F.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/UAV-741-F.jpg/250px-UAV-741-F.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="241" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/UAV-741-F.jpg/500px-UAV-741-F.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/97/UAV-741-F.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="482" /></a><figcaption>UEL UAV-741 Wankel engine for UAV operations, used on <a href="/wiki/AAI_RQ-7_Shadow" title="AAI RQ-7 Shadow">AAI RQ-7 Shadow</a></figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Flight_time_against_mass_of_small_drones.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Flight_time_against_mass_of_small_drones.svg/250px-Flight_time_against_mass_of_small_drones.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="333" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Flight_time_against_mass_of_small_drones.svg/500px-Flight_time_against_mass_of_small_drones.svg.png 1.5x" data-file-width="576" data-file-height="768" /></a><figcaption>Flight time against mass of small (less than 1&#160;kg) drones<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Nature&#95;-&#95;Future&#95;of&#95;sUAVs&#95;120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nature_-_Future_of_sUAVs-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<p>UAV endurance is not constrained by the physiological capabilities of a human pilot.
</p><p>Because of their small size, low weight, low vibration and high power-to-weight ratio, <a href="/wiki/Wankel_rotary_engines" class="mw-redirect" title="Wankel rotary engines">Wankel rotary engines</a> are used in many large UAVs. Their engine rotors cannot seize; the engine is not susceptible to shock-cooling during descent and it does not require an enriched fuel mixture for cooling at high power. These attributes reduce fuel usage, increasing range or payload.
</p><p>Proper drone cooling is essential for long-term drone endurance. Overheating and subsequent engine failure is the most common cause of drone failure.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_fuel_cells" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydrogen fuel cells">Hydrogen fuel cells</a>, using hydrogen power, may be able to extend the endurance of small UAVs, up to several hours.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>143<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Micro air vehicles endurance is so far best achieved with flapping-wing UAVs, followed by planes and multirotors standing last, due to lower <a href="/wiki/Reynolds_number" title="Reynolds number">Reynolds number</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Nature&#95;-&#95;Future&#95;of&#95;sUAVs&#95;120-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nature_-_Future_of_sUAVs-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Solar-electric UAVs, a concept originally championed by the AstroFlight Sunrise in 1974, have achieved flight times of several weeks.
</p><p>Solar-powered atmospheric satellites ("atmosats") designed for operating at altitudes exceeding 20&#160;km (12 miles, or 60,000 feet) for as long as five years could potentially perform duties more economically and with more versatility than <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">low Earth orbit</a> satellites. Likely applications include <a href="/wiki/Weather_drone" title="Weather drone">weather drones</a> for <a href="/wiki/Weather_reconnaissance" title="Weather reconnaissance">weather monitoring</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emergency_management#Recovery" title="Emergency management">disaster recovery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Earth_imaging" class="mw-redirect" title="Earth imaging">Earth imaging</a> and communications.
</p><p>Electric UAVs powered by microwave power transmission or laser power beaming are other potential endurance solutions.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>145<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Another application for a high endurance UAV would be to "stare" at a battlefield for a long interval (ARGUS-IS, Gorgon Stare, Integrated Sensor Is Structure) to record events that could then be played backwards to track battlefield activities.

td:nth-child(7),.mw-parser-output .col8center td:nth-child(8),.mw-parser-output .col9center td:nth-child(9),.mw-parser-output .col10center td:nth-child(10),.mw-parser-output .col11center <p>The delicacy of the British <a href="/wiki/PHASA-35" class="mw-redirect" title="PHASA-35">PHASA-35</a> military drone (at a late stage of development) is such that traversing the first turbulent twelve miles of atmosphere is a hazardous endeavor. It has, however, remained on station at 65,000 feet for 24 hours. Airbus' Zephyr in 2023 has attained 70,000 feet and flown for 64 days; 200 days aimed at. This is sufficiently close enough to <a href="/wiki/K%C3%A1rm%C3%A1n_line" title="Kármán line">near-space</a> for them to be regarded in "pseudo-satellites" as regards to their operational capabilities.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>155<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Reliability">Reliability</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Reliability"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Reliability improvements target all aspects of UAV systems, using <a href="/wiki/Resilience_(engineering_and_construction)" title="Resilience (engineering and construction)">resilience engineering</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fault_tolerance" title="Fault tolerance">fault tolerance</a> techniques.
</p><p>Individual reliability covers robustness of flight controllers, to ensure safety without excessive redundancy to minimize cost and weight.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>156<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Besides, dynamic assessment of <a href="/wiki/Flight_envelope" title="Flight envelope">flight envelope</a> allows damage-resilient UAVs, using <a href="/wiki/Nonlinear_system" title="Nonlinear system">non-linear analysis</a> with ad hoc designed loops or neural networks.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>157<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> UAV software liability is bending toward the design and certifications of <a href="/wiki/Avionics_software" title="Avionics software">crewed avionics software</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>158<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Swarm resilience involves maintaining operational capabilities and reconfiguring tasks given unit failures.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>159<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Applications">Applications</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Applications"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_unmanned_aerial_vehicle_applications" title="List of unmanned aerial vehicle applications">List of unmanned aerial vehicle applications</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:IRGC_Ground_New_Equipment_2021_(09).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/IRGC_Ground_New_Equipment_2021_%2809%29.jpg/250px-IRGC_Ground_New_Equipment_2021_%2809%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/IRGC_Ground_New_Equipment_2021_%2809%29.jpg/500px-IRGC_Ground_New_Equipment_2021_%2809%29.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="1050" data-file-height="700" /></a><figcaption>An Iranian <a href="/wiki/Qods_Mohajer-6" title="Qods Mohajer-6">Qods Mohajer-6</a> UCAV of the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Revolutionary_Guard_Corps_Ground_Forces" title="Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps Ground Forces">Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps Ground Forces</a> equipped with two <a href="/wiki/Qaem#Qaem_air-to-ground_bomb" title="Qaem">Qaem</a> <a href="/wiki/Precision-guided_munition" title="Precision-guided munition">precision-guided munition</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>In recent years, autonomous drones have begun to transform various application areas as they can fly beyond visual line of sight (BVLOS)<sup id="cite&#95;ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>160<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> while maximizing production, reducing costs and risks, ensuring site safety, security and regulatory compliance,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>161<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and protecting the human workforce in times of a pandemic.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>162<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> They can also be used for consumer-related missions like package delivery, as demonstrated by <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Prime_Air" title="Amazon Prime Air">Amazon Prime Air</a>, and critical deliveries of health supplies.
</p><p>There are numerous civilian, commercial, military, and aerospace applications for UAVs.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These include:
</p>
<dl><dt>General</dt>
<dd><a href="/wiki/Recreation" title="Recreation">Recreation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Disaster_relief" class="mw-redirect" title="Disaster relief">disaster relief</a>, <a href="/wiki/Archaeology" title="Archaeology">archeology</a>, conservation of <a href="/wiki/Conservation_biology" title="Conservation biology">biodiversity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Habitat_conservation" title="Habitat conservation">habitat</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>163<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement" title="Law enforcement">law enforcement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crime" title="Crime">crime</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Terrorism" title="Terrorism">terrorism</a>.</dd>
<dt>Commercial</dt>
<dd><a href="/wiki/Surveillance_aircraft" title="Surveillance aircraft">Aerial surveillance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Filmmaking" title="Filmmaking">filmmaking</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Mademlis2019&#95;164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mademlis2019-164"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>164<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Journalism" title="Journalism">journalism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scientific_method" title="Scientific method">scientific research</a>, <a href="/wiki/Surveying" title="Surveying">surveying</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freight_transport" title="Freight transport">cargo transport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mining" title="Mining">mining</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">manufacturing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">forestry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaic_power_station" title="Photovoltaic power station">solar farming</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thermal_power_station" title="Thermal power station">thermal energy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Port" title="Port">ports</a> and <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2025)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></dd></dl>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Warfare">Warfare</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Warfare"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Drone_warfare" title="Drone warfare">Drone warfare</a>, <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_combat_aerial_vehicle" title="Unmanned combat aerial vehicle">Unmanned combat aerial vehicle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Loitering_munition" title="Loitering munition">Loitering munition</a>, <a href="/wiki/One-way_attack_drone" title="One-way attack drone">One-way attack drone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_surveillance_and_reconnaissance_aerial_vehicle" title="Unmanned surveillance and reconnaissance aerial vehicle">Unmanned surveillance and reconnaissance aerial vehicle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miniature_UAV" title="Miniature UAV">Miniature UAV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Micro_air_vehicle" title="Micro air vehicle">Micro air vehicle</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Target_drone" title="Target drone">Target drone</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:2024-_Russian_drones_launched_against_Ukraine.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/2024-_Russian_drones_launched_against_Ukraine.svg/250px-2024-_Russian_drones_launched_against_Ukraine.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/2024-_Russian_drones_launched_against_Ukraine.svg/500px-2024-_Russian_drones_launched_against_Ukraine.svg.png 1.5x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="750" /></a><figcaption>In the <a href="/wiki/2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine" title="2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine">2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine</a>, use of Russian UAVs increased about tenfold from early 2024 through summer 2025.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-NYTimes&#95;20250908&#95;165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes_20250908-165"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>165<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayraktar_TB2_of_UAF,_2020,_09.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Bayraktar_TB2_of_UAF%2C_2020%2C_09.jpg/250px-Bayraktar_TB2_of_UAF%2C_2020%2C_09.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Bayraktar_TB2_of_UAF%2C_2020%2C_09.jpg/500px-Bayraktar_TB2_of_UAF%2C_2020%2C_09.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="900" /></a><figcaption>A <a href="/wiki/Baykar_Bayraktar_TB2" title="Baykar Bayraktar TB2">Baykar Bayraktar TB2</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Air_Force" title="Ukrainian Air Force">Ukrainian Air Force</a> armed with <a href="/wiki/MAM_(Smart_Micro_Munition)" class="mw-redirect" title="MAM (Smart Micro Munition)">MAM-L</a>; two <a href="/wiki/UAV_ground_control_station" title="UAV ground control station">ground control stations</a> in the background</figcaption></figure>
<p>As of 2020, seventeen countries have armed UAVs, and more than 100 countries use UAVs in a military capacity.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>166<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The first five countries producing domestic UAV designs are the Turkey, United States, China, Israel and Iran.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-BAYKAR,&#95;THE&#95;GLOBAL&#95;LEADER&#95;IN&#95;UCAV&#95;EXPORTS,&#95;ACHIEVES&#95;$1.8&#95;BILLION&#95;IN&#95;EXPORTS&#95;IN&#95;2024&#95;167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BAYKAR,_THE_GLOBAL_LEADER_IN_UCAV_EXPORTS,_ACHIEVES_$1.8_BILLION_IN_EXPORTS_IN_2024-167"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>167<span <a href="/wiki/Northrop_Grumman" title="Northrop Grumman">Northrop Grumman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Aerospace_Industries" title="Turkish Aerospace
