class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> China has established and expanded its presence in military UAV market<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ch&#95;171-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ch-171"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>171<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> since 2010. In the early 2020s, Turkey also established and expanded its presence in the military UAV market.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Strengthening&#95;Turkish&#95;Policy&#95;on&#95;Drone&#95;Exports&#95;168-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Strengthening_Turkish_Policy_on_Drone_Exports-168"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>168<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-ch&#95;171-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ch-171"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>171<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Turkey&#39;s&#95;defense&#95;industry&#95;targets&#95;more&#95;than&#95;$4&#95;billion&#95;in&#95;exports&#95;this&#95;year:&#95;Official&#95;169-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Turkey&#39;s_defense_industry_targets_more_than_$4_billion_in_exports_this_year:_Official-169"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>169<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Turkish&#95;defence&#95;industry&#95;grows&#95;as&#95;Akinci&#95;UCAV&#95;signs&#95;first&#95;export&#95;deal&#95;172-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Turkish_defence_industry_grows_as_Akinci_UCAV_signs_first_export_deal-172"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>172<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In the early 2010s, Israeli companies mainly focused on small surveillance UAV systems, and by the number of drones, Israel exported 60.7% (2014) of UAVs on the market while the United States exported 23.9% (2014).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Guardian&#95;report&#95;2015&#95;173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_report_2015-173"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>173<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Between 2010 and 2014, there were 439 drones exchanged compared to 322 in the five years previous to that, among these only small fraction of overall trade – just 11 (2.5%) of the 439 are armed drones.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Guardian&#95;report&#95;2015&#95;173-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_report_2015-173"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>173<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The US alone operated over 9,000 military UAVs in 2014; among them more than 7000 are <a href="/wiki/AeroVironment_RQ-11_Raven" title="AeroVironment RQ-11 Raven">RQ-11 Raven</a> <a href="/wiki/Miniature_UAV" title="Miniature UAV">miniature UAVs</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>174<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Since 2010, Chinese drone companies have begun to export large quantities of drones to the global military market. Of the 18 countries that are known to have received military drones between 2010 and 2019, the top 12 all purchased their drones from China.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ch&#95;171-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ch-171"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>171<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>175<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The shift accelerated in the 2020s due to China's advancement in drone technologies and manufacturing, compounded by market demand from the <a href="/wiki/Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian invasion of Ukraine">Russian invasion of Ukraine</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Gaza_war" title="Gaza war">Israel-Gaza conflict</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>176<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-wsj&#95;drone&#95;177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj_drone-177"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>177<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>178<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>For intelligence and reconnaissance missions, the inherent stealth of <a href="/wiki/Micro_air_vehicle" title="Micro air vehicle">micro UAV</a> flapping-wing <a href="/wiki/Ornithopter" title="Ornithopter">ornithopters</a>, imitating birds or insects, offers potential for covert surveillance and makes them difficult targets to bring down.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Unmanned_surveillance_and_reconnaissance_aerial_vehicle" title="Unmanned surveillance and reconnaissance aerial vehicle">Unmanned surveillance and reconnaissance aerial vehicle</a> are used for <a href="/wiki/Reconnaissance" title="Reconnaissance">reconnaissance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Offensive_(military)" title="Offensive (military)">attack</a>, <a href="/wiki/Demining" title="Demining">demining</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Target_practice" title="Target practice">target practice</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>179<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Following the 2022 <a href="/wiki/Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian invasion of Ukraine">Russian invasion of Ukraine</a>, a dramatic increase in UAV development took place with Ukraine creating the <a href="/wiki/Brave1" title="Brave1">Brave1</a> platform to promote rapid development of innovative systems. By 2025, <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_Systems_Forces_(Ukraine)" title="Unmanned Systems Forces (Ukraine)">Ukraine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_Systems_Forces_(Russia)" title="Unmanned Systems Forces (Russia)">Russia</a> had both established their own dedicated UAV military commands, named the <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_Systems_Forces" class="mw-disambig" title="Unmanned Systems Forces">Unmanned Systems Forces</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>180<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Unlike Russia, Ukraine has been able to innovatively employ UAVs to deliver equipment like flexible medical stretchers or electric bicycles to help evacuate wounded soldiers from combat.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>181<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>182<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Civil_applications">Civil applications</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Civil applications"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Zipline_Drone_Launch.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Zipline_Drone_Launch.jpg/250px-Zipline_Drone_Launch.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="172" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Zipline_Drone_Launch.jpg/500px-Zipline_Drone_Launch.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3570" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Zipline_(drone_delivery_company)" title="Zipline (drone delivery company)">Zipline's</a> aircraft being launched from a base in Rwanda to deliver blood products</figcaption></figure>
<p>The civilian (commercial and general) drone market is dominated by Chinese companies. Chinese manufacturer <a href="/wiki/DJI_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="DJI (company)">DJI</a> alone had 74% of the civil market share in 2018,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>183<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> with no other company accounting for more than 5%.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-market2018&#95;184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-market2018-184"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>184<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The companies continue to hold over 70% of global market share by 2023, despite under increasing scrutinies and sanctions from the United States.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>185<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The US Interior Department grounded its fleet of DJI drones in 2020, while the Justice Department prohibited the use of federal funds for the purchase of DJI and other foreign-made UAVs.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>186<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>187<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
DJI is followed by American company <a href="/wiki/3D_Robotics" title="3D Robotics">3D Robotics</a>, Chinese company <a href="/wiki/Yuneec_International" title="Yuneec International">Yuneec</a>, <a href="/wiki/Autel_Robotics" title="Autel Robotics">Autel Robotics</a>, and French company <a href="/wiki/Parrot_SA" title="Parrot SA">Parrot</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-market2018&#95;184-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-market2018-184"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>184<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>188<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2025, Chinese drone companies held 90% of the global UAV market share, with DJI accounting 80 percent of the world market.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>189<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>190<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>As of May 2021, 873,576 UAVs had been registered with the US <a href="/wiki/FAA" class="mw-redirect" title="FAA">FAA</a>, of which 42% were categorized as commercial and 58% as recreational.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>191<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 2018 NPD point to consumers increasingly purchasing drones with more advanced features with 33 percent growth in both the $500+ and $1000+ market segments.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>192<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The civil UAV market is relatively new compared to the military one. Companies are emerging in both developed and developing nations at the same time. Many early-stage startups have received support and funding from investors, as is the case in the United States, and from government agencies, as is the case in India.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>193<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Some universities offer research and training programs or degrees.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>194<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Private entities also provide online and in-person training programs for both recreational and commercial UAV use.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>195<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Consumer drones are widely used by police and military organizations worldwide because of the cost-effective nature of consumer products. Since 2018, the Israeli military have used DJI UAVs for light reconnaissance missions.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>196<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>197<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-wsj&#95;drone&#95;177-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj_drone-177"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>177<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> DJI drones have been used by Chinese police in <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a> since 2017<sup id="cite&#95;ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>198<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>199<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/American_police" class="mw-redirect" title="American police">American police</a> departments nationwide since 2018.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>200<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>201<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Both Ukraine and Russia used commercial DJI drones extensively during the <a href="/wiki/Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian invasion of Ukraine">Russian invasion of Ukraine</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-dji&#95;usage&#95;uk&#95;98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dji_usage_uk-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These civilian DJI drones were sourced by governments, hobbyists, international donations to Ukraine and Russia to support each side on the battlefield, and were often flown by drone hobbyists recruited by the armed forces. The prevalence of DJI drones was attributable to their market dominance, affordability, high performance, and reliability.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-fp&#95;2302&#95;99-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fp_2302-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>202<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Entertainment">Entertainment</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Entertainment"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Drone_art" title="Drone art">Drone art</a> and <a href="/wiki/Drone_racing" title="Drone racing">Drone racing</a></div>
<p>Drones are also used in nighttime <a href="/wiki/Drone_display" class="mw-redirect" title="Drone display">displays</a> for artistic and advertising purposes, with the main benefits being that they are safer, quieter, and better for the environment than fireworks. They can replace or be an adjunct to fireworks displays to reduce the financial burden of festivals. In addition they can complement fireworks due to the ability for drones to carry them, creating new forms of artwork in the process.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>203<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>204<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>205<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Drones can also be used for racing, either with or without VR functionality.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Aerial_photography">Aerial photography</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Aerial photography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Drone_journalism" title="Drone journalism">Drone journalism</a></div>
<p>Drones are ideally suited to capturing aerial shots in photography and cinematography, and are widely used for this purpose.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Mademlis2019&#95;164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mademlis2019-164"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>164<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Small drones avoid the need for precise coordination between pilot and cameraman, with the same person taking on both roles. Big drones with professional cine cameras usually have a drone pilot and a camera operator who controls the camera angle and lens. For example, the AERIGON cinema drone, used in film production, is operated by two people.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>206<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#What_information_to_include" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="A complete citation is needed. (December 2024)">full citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Drones provide access to dangerous, remote, or otherwise inaccessible sites.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Environmental_monitoring">Environmental monitoring</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Environmental monitoring"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>UASs or UAVs offer a great advantage for <a href="/wiki/Environmental_monitoring" title="Environmental monitoring">environmental monitoring</a> to generate a new generation of survey at very-high or ultra-high resolution both in space and time.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>207<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This gives the opportunity to bridge the existing gap between satellite data and field monitoring. This has stimulated a huge number of activities in order to enhance the description of natural and agricultural ecosystems. Most common applications are:
</p>
<ul><li>Topographic surveys<sup id="cite&#95;ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>208<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> for the production of orthomosaics, digital surface models and 3D models;</li>
<li>Monitoring of natural ecosystems for biodiversity monitoring,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>209<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> habitat mapping,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>210<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> detection of <a href="/wiki/Invasive_species" title="Invasive species">invasive alien species</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>211<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and study of ecosystem degradation due to invasive species or disturbances;</li>
<li>Precision agriculture<sup id="cite&#95;ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>212<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> which exploits all available technologies including UAV in order to produce more with less (e.g., optimisation of fertilizers, pesticides, irrigation);</li>
<li>River monitoring several methods have been developed to perform flow monitoring using image velocimetry methods which allow to properly describe the 2D flow velocity fields.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>213<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Structural integrity of any type of structure whether it be a dam, railway or other dangerous, inaccessible or massive locations for building monitoring.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>214<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Mineral detection for <a href="/wiki/Acid_mine_drainage" title="Acid mine drainage">acid mine drainage</a> using UAVs and <a href="/wiki/Hyperspectral_imaging" title="Hyperspectral imaging">hyperspectral</a> cameras can produce detailed maps of proxy minerals (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Goethite" title="Goethite">goethite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jarosite" title="Jarosite">jarosite</a>) for certain pH-values in natural, mining and post-mining environments, such as remediated sites.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>215<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>216<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In-situ gas measurements in potentially hazardous places like volcanic plumes.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>217<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<p>These activities can be completed with different measurements, such as <a href="/wiki/Photogrammetry" title="Photogrammetry">photogrammetry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thermography" title="Thermography">thermography</a>, multispectral images, 3D field scanning, <a href="/wiki/Gas_detectors" class="mw-redirect" title="Gas detectors">gas detectors</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Normalized_difference_vegetation_index" title="Normalized difference vegetation index">normalized difference vegetation index</a> maps.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Geological_hazards">Geological hazards</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Geological hazards"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>UAVs have become a widely used tool for studying <a href="/wiki/Geohazard" class="mw-redirect" title="Geohazard">geohazards</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Landslide" title="Landslide">landslides</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>218<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Various sensors, including radar, optical, and thermal, can be mounted on UAVs to monitor different properties. UAVs enable the capture of images of various <a href="/wiki/Landslide" title="Landslide">landslide</a> features, such as transverse, radial, and longitudinal cracks, ridges, scarps, and surfaces of rupture, even in inaccessible areas of the sliding mass.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>219<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>220<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Moreover, processing the optical images captured by UAVs also allows for the creation of <a href="/wiki/Point_cloud" title="Point cloud">point clouds</a> and 3D models, from which these properties can be derived.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>221<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Comparing <a href="/wiki/Point_cloud" title="Point cloud">point clouds</a> obtained at different times allows for the detection of changes caused by landslide deformation.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>222<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>223<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Mineral_exploration">Mineral exploration</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Mineral exploration"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>UAVs may help in the discovery of new or reevaluation of known <a href="/wiki/Mineral_Deposit" class="mw-redirect" title="Mineral Deposit">mineral deposits</a> to meet the demand for <a href="/wiki/Raw_material" title="Raw material">raw materials</a> such as critical raw metals (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Cobalt" title="Cobalt">cobalt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nickel" title="Nickel">nickel</a>), <a href="/wiki/Rare-earth_element" title="Rare-earth element">rare earths</a> and battery minerals. By employing a suite of sensors (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Spectral_imaging" title="Spectral imaging">spectral imaging</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lidar" title="Lidar">Lidar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magnetism" title="Magnetism">magnetics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gamma_spectroscopy" title="Gamma spectroscopy">gamma-ray spectroscopy</a>),<sup id="cite&#95;ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>224<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>225<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and similar to those used in environmental monitoring, UAV-based data can produce maps of geological surface and subsurface features, contributing to more efficient and targeted mineral exploration.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>226<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>227<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Agriculture,_forestry_and_environmental_studies"><span id="Agriculture.2C_forestry_and_environmental_studies"></span>Agriculture, forestry and environmental studies</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Agriculture, forestry and environmental studies"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_drone" title="Agricultural drone">Agricultural drone</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Drone_crop_fertilizer.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Drone_crop_fertilizer.jpg/250px-Drone_crop_fertilizer.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="328" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Drone_crop_fertilizer.jpg/500px-Drone_crop_fertilizer.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="1662" data-file-height="2182" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Agricultural_drone" title="Agricultural drone">Agricultural drone</a> on trailer setup</figcaption></figure>
<p>As global demand for food production grows exponentially, resources are depleted, farmland is reduced, and agricultural labor is increasingly in short supply, there is an urgent need for more convenient and smarter agricultural solutions than traditional methods, and the agricultural drone and robotics industry is expected to make progress.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>228<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Agricultural drones have been used to help build sustainable agriculture all over the world leading to a new generation of agriculture.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>229<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In this context, there is a proliferation of innovations in both tools and methodologies which allow precise description of vegetation state and also may help to precisely distribute nutrients, pesticides or seeds over a field.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Manfreda&#95;Dor&#95;Remote&#95;sensing&#95;7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Manfreda_Dor_Remote_sensing-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The use of UAVs is also being investigated to help detect and fight wildfires, whether through observation or launching pyrotechnic devices to start <a href="/wiki/Controlled_burn" title="Controlled burn">backfires</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>230<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>UAVs are also now widely used to survey wildlife such as nesting seabirds, seals and even wombat burrows.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>231<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Law_enforcement">Law enforcement</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Law enforcement"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Use_of_UAVs_in_law_enforcement" class="mw-redirect" title="Use of UAVs in law enforcement">Use of UAVs in law enforcement</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Police" title="Police">Police</a> can use drones for applications such as <a href="/wiki/Search_and_rescue" title="Search and rescue">search and rescue</a> and <a href="/wiki/Traffic_monitoring" class="mw-redirect" title="Traffic monitoring">traffic monitoring</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>232<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Humanitarian_aid">Humanitarian aid</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Humanitarian aid"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Delivery_drone" title="Delivery drone">Delivery drone</a></div>
<p>Drones are increasingly finding their application in humanitarian aid and disaster relief, where they are used for a wide range of applications such as delivering food, medicine and essential items to remote areas or image mapping before and following disasters.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>233<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Safety_and_security">Safety and security</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Safety and security"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_UAV-related_incidents" class="mw-redirect" title="List of UAV-related incidents">List of UAV-related incidents</a> and <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_combat_aerial_vehicle" title="Unmanned combat aerial vehicle">Unmanned combat aerial vehicle</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:USDA_Drone_poster.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/USDA_Drone_poster.jpg/250px-USDA_Drone_poster.jpg" decoding="async" width="230" height="288" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/USDA_Drone_poster.jpg/500px-USDA_Drone_poster.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="3000" /></a><figcaption>US Department of Agriculture poster warning about the risks of flying UAVs near wildfires</figcaption></figure>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Threats">Threats</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Threats"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Nuisance">Nuisance</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Nuisance"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>UAVs can threaten airspace security in numerous ways, including unintentional collisions or other interference with other aircraft, deliberate attacks or by distracting pilots or flight controllers. The first incident of a drone-airplane collision occurred in mid-October 2017 in Quebec City, Canada.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>234<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The first recorded instance of a drone collision with a <a href="/wiki/Hot_air_balloon" title="Hot air balloon">hot air balloon</a> occurred on 10 August 2018 in <a href="/wiki/Driggs,_Idaho" title="Driggs, Idaho">Driggs, Idaho</a>, United States; although there was no significant damage to the balloon nor any injuries to its three occupants, the balloon pilot reported the incident to the <a href="/wiki/National_Transportation_Safety_Board" title="National Transportation Safety Board">National Transportation Safety Board</a>, stating that "I hope this incident helps create a conversation of respect for nature, the airspace, and rules and regulations".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>235<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Unauthorized UAV flights into or near major airports have prompted extended shutdowns of commercial flights.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>236<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Drones caused <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport_drone_incident" title="Gatwick Airport drone incident">significant disruption at Gatwick Airport during December 2018</a>, needing the deployment of the British Army.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-2018-12-01-j-post&#95;237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018-12-01-j-post-237"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>237<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-2018-12-20-guardian&#95;238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018-12-20-guardian-238"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>238<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In the United States, flying close to a wildfire is punishable by a maximum $25,000 fine. Nonetheless, in 2014 and 2015, firefighting air support in California was hindered on several occasions, including at the <a href="/wiki/Lake_Fire_(2015)" title="Lake Fire (2015)">Lake Fire</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-atc&#95;239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atc-239"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>239<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/North_Fire" class="mw-redirect" title="North Fire">North Fire</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>240<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>241<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In response, California legislators introduced a bill that would allow firefighters to disable UAVs which invaded restricted airspace.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>242<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The FAA later required registration of most UAVs.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Security_vulnerabilities">Security vulnerabilities</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Security vulnerabilities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>By 2017, drones were being used to drop contraband into prisons.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>243<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
</p><p>The interest in UAVs cybersecurity has been raised greatly after the Predator UAV video stream hijacking incident in 2009,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>244<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> where Islamic militants used cheap, off-the-shelf equipment to stream video feeds from a UAV. Another risk is the possibility of hijacking or jamming a UAV in flight. Several security researchers have made public some vulnerabilities in commercial UAVs, in some cases even providing full source code or tools to reproduce their attacks.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>245<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> At a workshop on UAVs and privacy in October 2016, researchers from the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Trade_Commission" title="Federal Trade Commission">Federal Trade Commission</a> showed they were able to hack into three different consumer <a href="/wiki/Quadcopter" title="Quadcopter">quadcopters</a> and noted that UAV manufacturers can make their UAVs more secure by the basic security measures of encrypting the Wi-Fi signal and adding password protection.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>246<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Aggression">Aggression</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Aggression"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Many UAVs have been loaded with dangerous payloads, and/or crashed into targets. Payloads have included or could include explosives, chemical, radiological or biological hazards. UAVs with generally non-lethal payloads could possibly be hacked and put to malicious purposes. Counter-UAV systems (C-UAS), from detection to electronic warfare to UAVs designed to destroy other UAVs, are in development and being deployed by states to counter this threat.
</p><p>Such developments have occurred despite the difficulties. As J. Rogers stated in a 2017 interview to A&amp;T, "There is a big debate out there at the moment about what the best way is to counter these small UAVs, whether they are used by hobbyists causing a bit of a nuisance or in a more sinister manner by a terrorist actor".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>247<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Countermeasures">Countermeasures</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Countermeasures"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Counter_unmanned_air_system">Counter unmanned air system</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Counter unmanned air system"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Electronic_warfare" title="Electronic warfare">Electronic warfare</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Italian_Army_-_17th_Anti-aircraft_Artillery_Regiment_%22Sforzesca%22_troops_with_CPM-Drone_Jammer.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Italian_Army_-_17th_Anti-aircraft_Artillery_Regiment_%22Sforzesca%22_troops_with_CPM-Drone_Jammer.jpg/250px-Italian_Army_-_17th_Anti-aircraft_Artillery_Regiment_%22Sforzesca%22_troops_with_CPM-Drone_Jammer.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Italian_Army_-_17th_Anti-aircraft_Artillery_Regiment_%22Sforzesca%22_troops_with_CPM-Drone_Jammer.jpg/500px-Italian_Army_-_17th_Anti-aircraft_Artillery_Regiment_%22Sforzesca%22_troops_with_CPM-Drone_Jammer.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="2527" data-file-height="1687" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Italian_Army" title="Italian Army">Italian Army</a> soldiers of the 17th Anti-aircraft Artillery Regiment "Sforzesca" with a portable drone jammer in <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a></figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Cannon_support_of_anti-drone_complex_%22Rat%60h%22_on_the_SBA-70K2_chassis_(front_view).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Cannon_support_of_anti-drone_complex_%22Rat%60h%22_on_the_SBA-70K2_chassis_%28front_view%29.jpg/250px-Cannon_support_of_anti-drone_complex_%22Rat%60h%22_on_the_SBA-70K2_chassis_%28front_view%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="164" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Cannon_support_of_anti-drone_complex_%22Rat%60h%22_on_the_SBA-70K2_chassis_%28front_view%29.jpg/500px-Cannon_support_of_anti-drone_complex_%22Rat%60h%22_on_the_SBA-70K2_chassis_%28front_view%29.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="4896" data-file-height="3207" /></a><figcaption>Cannon anti-drone system</figcaption></figure>
<p>The malicious use of UAVs has led to the development of <a href="/wiki/Anti-aircraft_warfare#Anti-UAV_defences" title="Anti-aircraft warfare">counter unmanned air system</a> (C-UAS) technologies. Automatic tracking and detection of UAVs from commercial cameras have become accurate thanks to the development of deep learning based machine learning algorithms.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-issacmedina21unmanned&#95;248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-issacmedina21unmanned-248"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>248<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is also possible to automatically identify UAVs across different cameras with different viewpoints and hardware specification with re-identification methods.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-organisciak22uavreid&#95;249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-organisciak22uavreid-249"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>249<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Commercial systems such as the Aaronia AARTOS have been installed on major international airports.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>250<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>251<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Once a UAV is detected, it can be countered with kinetic force (missiles, projectiles or another UAV) or by non-kinetic force (laser, microwaves, communications jamming).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>252<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Anti-aircraft missile systems such as the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Dome" title="Iron Dome">Iron Dome</a> are also being enhanced with C-UAS technologies. Utilising a smart UAV swarm to counter one or more hostile UAVs is also proposed.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-hartley21formation&#95;253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hartley21formation-253"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>253<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A variety of counter-UAS (C-UAS) systems have been developed globally to address the growing threat of small and tactical UAVs. These include multi-layered approaches combining radar, electro-optical sensors, radio frequency detection, and jamming technologies. Among them are systems developed by <a href="/wiki/Elbit_Systems" title="Elbit Systems">Elbit Systems</a>, such as the ReDrone™ suite,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>254<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>255<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> which includes both fixed and portable configurations for detection and mitigation of drones in civilian and military environments. The Red Sky 2 system, also developed by Elbit, integrates multiple sensors and effectors and is designed to protect strategic sites from low-altitude aerial threats.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>256<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Other developers, such as AirSight, specialize in the software and systems integration layer of C-UAS, utilizing AI and machine learning to analyze sensor data for drone detection and threat assessment in complex environments, as demonstrated by the launch of their AirGuard V3.18 system.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-auto2&#95;127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-127"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Regulation">Regulation</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Regulation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Regulation_of_unmanned_aerial_vehicles" title="Regulation of unmanned aerial vehicles">Regulation of unmanned aerial vehicles</a></div>
<p>Regulatory bodies around the world are developing <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_aircraft_system_traffic_management" title="Unmanned aircraft system traffic management">unmanned aircraft system traffic management</a> solutions to better integrate UAVs into airspace.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>257<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The use of unmanned aerial vehicles is becoming increasingly regulated by the <a href="/wiki/Civil_aviation_authority" title="Civil aviation authority">civil aviation authorities</a> of individual countries. Regulatory regimes can differ significantly according to drone size and use. The <a href="/wiki/International_Civil_Aviation_Organization" title="International Civil Aviation Organization">International Civil Aviation Organization (ICAO)</a> began exploring the use of drone technology as far back as 2005, which resulted in a 2011 report.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>258<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> France was among the first countries to set a national framework based on this report and larger aviation bodies such as the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">FAA</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Aviation_Safety_Agency" class="mw-redirect" title="European Aviation Safety Agency">EASA</a> quickly followed suit.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>259<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2021, the FAA published a rule requiring all commercially used UAVs and all UAVs regardless of intent weighing 250 g or more to participate in <a href="/wiki/Remote_ID" title="Remote ID">Remote ID</a>, which makes drone locations, controller locations, and other information public from takeoff to shutdown; this rule has since been challenged in the pending federal lawsuit <i><a href="/wiki/RaceDayQuads_v._FAA" title="RaceDayQuads v. FAA">RaceDayQuads v. FAA</a></i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>260<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>261<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="EU_Drone_Certification_–_Class_Identification_Label"><span id="EU_Drone_Certification_.E2.80.93_Class_Identification_Label"></span>EU Drone Certification – Class Identification Label</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: EU Drone Certification – Class Identification Label"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The implementation of the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://eudroneport.com/blog/uas-class-label/">Class Identification Label</a> serves a crucial purpose in the regulation and operation of drones.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>262<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The label is a verification mechanism designed to confirm that drones within a specific class meet the rigorous standards set by administrations for design and manufacturing.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>263<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These standards are necessary to ensure the safety and reliability of drones in various industries and applications.
</p><p>By providing this assurance to customers, the Class Identification Label helps to increase confidence in drone technology and encourages wider adoption across industries. This, in turn, contributes to the growth and development of the drone industry and supports the integration of drones into society.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Export_controls">Export controls</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Unmanned_aerial_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Export controls"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The export of UAVs or technology capable of carrying a 500&#160;kg payload at least 300&#160;km is restricted in many countries by the <a href="/wiki/Missile_Technology_Control_Regime" title="Missile Technology Control Regime">Missile Technology Control Regime</a>.
</p>
